<![endif]--></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Concentration</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Divine Life Society Publication: </b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/teachings/concentration.htm"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Concentration</b></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Sri Swami Sivananda</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">If you focus the rays of the sun through a lens, they can burn cotton or a piece of paper; but, the scattered rays cannot do this act. If you want to talk to a man at a distance, you make a funnel of your hand and speak. The sound-waves are collected at one point and then directed towards the man. He can hear your speech very clearly. The water is converted into steam and the steam is concentrated at a point. The railway engine moves. All these are instances of concentrated waves. Even so, if you collect the dissipated rays of the mind and focus them at a point, you will have wonderful concentration. The concentrated mind will serve as a potent searchlight to find out the treasures of the soul and attain the supreme wealth of Atman (the Self), eternal bliss, immortality and perennial joy. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Real <a href="http://www.dlshq.org/teachings/rajayoga.htm">Raja Yoga</a> starts from concentration. Concentration merges in meditation. Concentration is a portion of meditation. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Meditation follows concentration. Samadhi (superconscious state) follows mediation. The Jivanmukti (liberated being) state follows the attainment of Nirvikalpa Samadhi which is free from all thoughts of duality. Jivanmukti leads to emancipation from the wheel of birth and death. Therefore, concentration is the first and foremost thing a Sadhaka or aspirant should acquire in the spiritual path. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">You are born to concentrate the mind on God after collecting the mental rays that are dissipated on various objects. That is your important duty. You forget the duty on account of Moha (infatuation) for family, children, money, power, position, respect, name and fame. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Concentration of the mind on God after purification can give you real happiness and knowledge. You are born for this purpose only. You are carried away to external objects through attachment and infatuated love. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><a name="what"><b>WHAT IS CONCENTRATION?</b></a></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Once a Sanskrit scholar approached Kabir and asked him, O Kabir, what are you doing now?". Kabir replied, "O Pundit, I am detaching the mind from worldly objects and attaching it to the lotus-feet of the Lord". This is concentration. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Concentration or Dharana is centering the mind on one single thought. Vedantins try to fix the mind on the Atman. This is their Dharana. Hatha Yogins and Raja Yogins concentrate their mind on the six Chakras (energy centres). Bhaktas concentrate on their Ishta Devata (tutelary diety). Concentration is a great necessity for all aspirants. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">During concentration, the various rays of the mind are collected and focussed on the object of concentration. There will be no tossing of the mind. One idea occupies the mind. The whole energy of the mind is concentrated on that one idea. The senses become still. They do not function. When there is deep concentration, there is no consciousness of the body and surroundings. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">When you study a book with profound interest, you do not hear if a man shouts and calls you by your name. You do not see a person when he stands in front of you. You do not smell the sweet fragrance of flowers that are placed on the table by your side. This is concentration or one-pointedness of mind. The mind is fixed firmly on one thing. You must have such a deep concentration when you think of God or the Atman. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Everybody possesses some ability to concentrate. Everybody does concentrate to a certain extent when he reads a book, when he writes a letter, when he plays tennis, and in fact, when he does any kind of work. But, for spiritual purposes, concentration should be developed to an infinite degree. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">There is great concentration when you play cards or chess, but the mind is not filled with pure and divine thoughts. The mental contents are of an undesirable nature. You can hardly experience the divine thrill, ecstasy, and elevation when the mind is filled with impure thoughts. Every object has its own mental associations. You will have to fill up the mind with sublime, spiritual thoughts. Then only the mind will be expurgated of all worldly thoughts. The picture of <a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/jesus.htm">Lord Jesus</a> or <a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/buddha.htm">Buddha</a> or Lord Krishna is associated with sublime, soul-stirring ideas; chess and cards are associated with ideas of gambling, cheating and so forth. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><a name="objects"><b>OBJECTS OF CONCENTRATION</b></a></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Sit on any comfortable pose. Place a picture of your Ishta Devata in front of you. Look at the picture with a steady gaze. Then close your eyes and visualise the picture in the centre of your heart or in the space between the eyebrows. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">When the picture fades out in your mental vision, open the eyes and gaze at the picture again. Close your eyes after a few seconds and repeat the process. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">It is easy to concentrate the mind on external objects. The mind has a natural tendency to go outwards. In the beginning stage of practice, you can concentrate on a black dot. on the wall, a candle flame, a bright star, the moon, or any other object that is pleasing to the mind. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The mind should be trained to concentrate on gross objects in the beginning; and later on, you can successfully concentrate on subtle objects and abstract ideas. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">There is no concentration without something to rest the mind upon. Concentrate on anything that appeals to you as good or anything which the mind likes best. It is very difficult to fix the mind, in the beginning, on any object which the mind dislikes. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Practise various sorts of concentration. This will train or discipline your mind wonderfully. Now concentrate on the Himalayas, a very great object. Then concentrate on a mustard or a pin-point. Now concentrate on a distant object. Then concentrate on a near object. Now concentrate on a colour, sound, touch, smell, or taste. Now concentrate on the virtue mercy. Then concentrate on the virtue 'patience'. Now concentrate on the Sloka, <i>"Jyotishamai Tat Jyotih</i>. Then concentrate on <i>"Satyam Jnanam Anantam"</i>. Now concentrate on the im<a name="_GoBack"></a>age of Lord Siva. Then concentrate on the Aham Brahmasmi" Mahavakya. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;" class="MsoHyperlink"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Excerpts from:</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/teachings/concentration.htm"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Concentration</b></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Sri Swami Sivananda</b></span><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
